<p>By June 2016, Nintendo reported lifetime sales of 13.36¬†million Wii U console units and 92.35 million software units worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hardware_Software_Sales_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hardware_Software_Sales-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch">Launch</span></h3>
<p>During its first week of release in the United States, Nintendo sold its entire allotment of over 400,000 units<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NintenHardware_cnet_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-NintenHardware_cnet-167">[165]</a></sup> and sold a total of 425,000 units for the month of November, according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NPD_Group" title="NPD Group">NPD Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPD_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPD-168">[166]</a></sup> It also sold over 40,000 consoles in the UK in its first weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK-169">[167]</a></sup> In Japan, over 600,000 Wii U units were sold during December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan-170">[168]</a></sup> Nearly 890,000 Wii U units were sold in the United States after 41 days on the market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NintenHardware_register_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-NintenHardware_register-171">[169]</a></sup> From the Wii U's launch till December 31, 2012, Nintendo reported that 3.06 million consoles and 11.69 million software units had been shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendosales_Q3_2013_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendosales_Q3_2013-154">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2013, Nintendo sold 57,000 Wii U units in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> By comparison, the original <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> sold 435,000 in January 2007, also two months after launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-January2013NPDSalesCNET_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-January2013NPDSalesCNET-173">[171]</a></sup> Initial sales numbers in the US and other territories were lower than expected, resulting in Nintendo cutting sales projections for <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2013 by 17 percent, from 5.5 million to 4 million;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> the system actually ended up selling 3.5 million units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012sales_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-2012sales-175">[173]</a></sup> During the first quarter of 2013, Nintendo reported that 390,000 consoles and 1.73 million software units were shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendosales_Q1_2013_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendosales_Q1_2013-152">[150]</a></sup> From March to June 2013, the system sold approximately 160,000 units, which was down 51 percent from the three months prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcsales_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsales-176">[174]</a></sup> During the second quarter of 2013, Nintendo reported that 160,000 consoles and 1.03 million software units were shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendosales_Q2_2013_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendosales_Q2_2013-153">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_support">Loss of support</span></h3>
<p>In May 2013, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> announced that it was reducing support for the Wii U and had no games in development for it,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ea_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-ea-177">[175]</a></sup> but then partially reconsidered this decision a few days later, with EA's CFO announcing that "We are building titles for the Nintendo console, but not anywhere near as many as we are for PlayStation or Xbox".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2013" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2013">E3 2013</a>, Ubisoft revealed that they were not going to make any more exclusives for the Wii U until sales of the console improved,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> though they stated shortly after that they are still "big supporters" of the Wii U, and plan to release as many Wii U games in 2013 as they did in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> In July 2013, <a href="/wiki/Bethesda_Softworks" title="Bethesda Softworks">Bethesda Softworks</a> announced that they had no games in development for the Wii U, with Bethesda VP of PR and marketing Pete Hines explaining: "It depends on the games that we are making and how we think it aligns with that console, and how the hardware aligns with the other stuff we are making".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> This explanation was later refined to being largely due to the hardware.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> Contrarily, <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a> has stated that they will "do everything they can" to support the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of July 2013, <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a>, the second-largest supermarket chain in the UK, confirmed that they had no plans to stock the Wii U, but would still stock games "on a title by title merit basis".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> Despite this, many specialist retailers continued to emphasize their support, with <a href="/wiki/Game_(retailer)" title="Game (retailer)">Game</a> CEO Martyn Gibbs saying "We fully support all Nintendo products, including Wii U."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Price_cut_and_first-party_titles">Price cut and first-party titles</span></h3>
<p>Following the system's $50 price cut and the release of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Zelda:_The_Wind_Waker_HD" title="The Legend of Zelda: The Wind Waker HD">The Legend of Zelda: The Wind Waker HD</a></i> on September 20, 2013, Wii U sales in North America saw a 200% rise over August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> From July to September 2013, the system sold approximately 300,000 units, which was up 87 percent from the three months prior. Despite only having sold 460,000 consoles since April, Nintendo maintained its 9 million Wii U sales forecast for the fiscal year through March 2014. Wii U software showed improvement in the Q2 period, reaching 5.27 million units, a 400 percent jump on the previous quarter. Nintendo credited the software growth to key first-party releases like <i><a href="/wiki/Pikmin_3" title="Pikmin 3">Pikmin 3</a></i> and <i>The Legend of Zelda: The Wind Waker HD</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> During the third quarter of 2013, Nintendo reported that 300,000 consoles and 5.27 million software units were shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendosales_Q3_2013_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-nintendosales_Q3_2013-154">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2013, online retailer <i>Play.com</i> announced that its Wii U sales saw a 75% sales increase. The company also predicted that the Wii U would be more popular than its competition, the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>, among children during the holiday season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> Following the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Wii_Party_U" title="Wii Party U">Wii Party U</a></i> on October 31 in Japan, weekly Wii U sales spiked to 38,802 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> On November 29, 2013, Nintendo of France deputy general manager Philippe Lavou√© announced that the Wii U had sold approximately 175,000 units in France since launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> During the first two weeks of December, the Wii U was the top performing home console in Japan, with 123,665 units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> After one year in the market, the Wii U had sold approximately 150,000 units in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NPD_Group" title="NPD Group">NPD Group</a>, Wii U sales in November increased by 340 percent over sales in October in North America, selling approximately 220,700 units sold in that month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> According to several publications, including NPD Group, December 2013 was the best-selling Wii U month in the US since its launch, selling around 481,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> Independent estimates put the number of Wii U consoles sold by the end of 2013 between 4.5 and 5.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> During the fourth quarter of 2013, Nintendo reported that 1.95 million consoles and 9.96 million software units were shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendosales_Q4_2013_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendosales_Q4_2013-155">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2014, citing lower-than-expected sales during the 2013 holiday season, Nintendo announced that Wii U sales forecasts for fiscal year 2014 had been cut from 9 million units to 2.8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup> In light of this announcement, the Wii U's long-term viability has been called into question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> In February 2014, Nintendo revealed that the Wii U had improved about 180% in year-over-year sales in the United States due to the launch of <i><a href="/wiki/Donkey_Kong_Country:_Tropical_Freeze" title="Donkey Kong Country: Tropical Freeze">Donkey Kong Country: Tropical Freeze</a></i>, which sold 130,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> By February 26, Wii U sales had surpassed those of the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> In March 2014, Nintendo sold just over 70,000 Wii U units, tracking it down 50% less than the <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> and 90% less than the <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> during equivalent time periods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup> During the month, total worldwide sales of the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> surpassed those of the Wii U.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup> During the first quarter of 2014, Nintendo reported that 310,000 consoles and 2.91 million software units were shipped worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nintendosales_Q1_2014_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-nintendosales_Q1_2014-156">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>During an annual investors' meeting, Satoru Iwata revealed Nintendo's projection of 3.6 million Wii U unit sales during the fiscal year ending March 2015<span style="display:none">¬†(<span class="dtend">March 2015</span>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup> On May 22, 2014, Nintendo France announced that sales were 50% higher compared to the last year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup> With <i>Mario Kart 8</i> being Nintendo's biggest game launch,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> Wii U console sales reportedly increased by 666% in the United Kingdom, with the <i>Mario Kart 8</i> console bundle representing 82% of the region's Wii U console sales for the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MK8_UK_hardware_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-MK8_UK_hardware-205">[203]</a></sup> NPD Group reported that in the United States, when comparing the month of June 2013 to the same month in 2014, Wii U software sales were up 373% and console sales were up 233%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>The record would be surpassed in November 2014 by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._for_Wii_U" title="Super Smash Bros. for Wii U">Super Smash Bros. for Wii U</a></i>, which sold 490,000 copies in the United States during its first three days of availability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cvg-smashwiiusales_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-cvg-smashwiiusales-131">[129]</a></sup> According to Nintendo of America, December 2014 was Wii U's biggest month in terms of sales in the United States. Hardware sales increased 29%, and software sales increased 75% in comparison to December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2015, Nintendo announced that as of the end of fiscal third quarter 2015, and nearly three years following its launch, it had shipped over 10 million Wii U units worldwide. However, sales of Wii U units during this quarter were down in comparison to the same quarter in 2014, with 470,000 units sold (in comparison to 510,000 in 2014). In comparison, PlayStation 4 and Xbox One had each yielded sales of 10 million units after approximately one year from their respective launches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnet-10mwiiu_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnet-10mwiiu-208">[206]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_of_Nintendo_Switch">Impact of Nintendo Switch</span></h3>
<p>The future of the Wii U was left unclear with Nintendo's announcement of a new console platform codenamed <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">NX</a>, which was scheduled to be launched worldwide in March 2017. Nintendo stated that NX would have a "brand-new concept", and not be a direct successor to the Wii U or <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">3DS</a> product lines; in an interview with the <i><a href="/wiki/Asahi_Shimbun" title="Asahi Shimbun">Asahi Shimbun</a></i>, company president <a href="/wiki/Tatsumi_Kimishima" title="Tatsumi Kimishima">Tatsumi Kimishima</a> reiterated this position and stated that while he thinks that the Wii U business would "slow" after the release of NX, he felt that the console would "have a larger impact than the Wii U".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vg247-nxsuccessor_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-vg247-nxsuccessor-209">[207]</a></sup> The announcement that <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Zelda:_Breath_of_the_Wild" title="The Legend of Zelda: Breath of the Wild">The Legend of Zelda: Breath of the Wild</a></i> was in development for both Wii U and NX further supported Nintendo's view of the console as being a new product line, rather than a replacement for its existing hardware.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geekcom-wontreplace_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-geekcom-wontreplace-210">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CnetNX_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-CnetNX-211">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ign-zelda17_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-ign-zelda17-213">[211]</a></sup> In a shareholders report in July 2016, Kimishima and Miyamoto stated that they had expected the Wii U to sell 100 million units, comparable to the success of the Wii, but with only 13 million units sold worldwide, they would now need to rely on NX to make up for losses on Wii U sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new platform, now known as <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">Nintendo Switch</a>, was officially announced on October 20, 2016; it is a <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet</a>-like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hybrid_video_game_console" title="Hybrid video game console">hybrid video game console</a> with detachable controllers, and the ability to be placed in a <a href="/wiki/Docking_station" title="Docking station">docking station</a> with an output to allow games to be played on a television. Although it is a hybrid device capable of being used as both a portable and home console, Nintendo officially positioned the platform as "a home gaming system first and foremost". Following the unveiling, a Nintendo spokesperson confirmed that the company would slow production of Wii U hardware, stating that "as we prepare for the launch of Nintendo Switch in March of 2017, Nintendo will ship 800,000 Wii U hardware units to the global market for this fiscal year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon-homefirst2_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-homefirst2-215">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[214]</a></sup> In mid-November 2016, Nintendo announced that Japanese production of the Wii U would be ending "in the near future", and that shipments to the North American and European markets for the year had already been sent out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[215]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time Magazine</a></i> in January 2017, <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Fils-Aim%C3%A9" title="Reggie Fils-Aim√©">Reggie Fils-Aim√©</a> commented that the system was "a necessary step, in order to get to Nintendo Switch." Fils-Aim√© also compared the system to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nintendo_GameCube" title="Nintendo GameCube">Nintendo GameCube</a>, claiming that the Wii U will be remembered fondly despite its relatively poor sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[216]</a></sup> During a press event for the Switch in New York City, he also stated that <i>Breath of the Wild</i> would be Nintendo's final first-party title for Wii U.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-polygon-lastgame_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-polygon-lastgame-219">[217]</a></sup></p>
